# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

Perfect! I've completed the analysis and created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings on HTTP filter factory registration and instantiation in Envoy v1.31.2.

## Summary

The trace covers the complete HTTP filter factory lifecycle:

### **Key Components:**

1. **Filter Factory Registry** - `Registry::FactoryRegistry<NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory>` stores and retrieves filter factories by type

2. **Core Interfaces** (envoy/http/filter_factory.h and envoy/server/filter_config.h):
   - `FilterFactoryCb` - callback function that instantiates filters
   - `FilterChainManager` - per-connection interface for filter creation
   - `FilterChainFactory` - creates filter chains for streams
   - `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` - filter configuration factory interface

3. **Configuration Processing** (source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.h/cc):
   - `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` implements `FilterChainFactory`
   - Uses `FilterChainHelper::processFilters()` to build filter factory list

4. **Per-Connection Instantiation** (source/common/http/filter_manager.h/cc):
   - `FilterManager` implements `FilterChainManager`
   - `createFilterChain()` assembles filters when streams arrive
   - `applyFilterFactoryCb()` invokes factory callbacks to instantiate filters

5. **Dynamic Configuration** (source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h):
   - `HttpDynamicFilterConfigProviderImpl` manages runtime filter config updates
   - `instantiateFilterFactory()` creates updated factory callbacks from xDS configs

The answer file provides all relevant files, symbols, and the complete call chain showing how filters flow from registration through per-request instantiation.

follows a two-stage model: static registration at initialization and per-connection instantiation at runtime.\\n\\n### 1. Filter Factory Registry and Registration\\n\\n**Core Interface** (envoy/server/filter_config.h):\\n- `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` - Base interface for HTTP filter factories. Each HTTP filter implements a config factory that extends this interface.\\n- `UpstreamHttpFilterConfigFactory` - Parallel interface for upstream-specific HTTP filters.\\n\\nFilters are registered statically using `Registry::RegisterFactory<FilterConfigType, NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory>()`. The registry (Registry::FactoryRegistry<NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory>) stores factories indexed by their type name.\\n\\n### 2. Factory Callback and Filter Instantiation\\n\\n**Core Types** (envoy/http/filter_factory.h):\\n- `FilterFactoryCb` - Function type `std::function<void(FilterChainFactoryCallbacks&)>` that creates and installs filters for a stream. Factories return this callback during initialization.\\n- `FilterChainManager` - Abstract interface with `applyFilterFactoryCb()` method, implemented per-connection to manage filter instantiation.\\n- `FilterChainFactory` - Interface for creating filter chains, with `createFilterChain()` called when new streams arrive.\\n\\n### 3. Configuration and Filter Chain Creation\\n\\n**Configuration Processing** (source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.h and config.cc):\\n- `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` implements `Http::FilterChainFactory`.\\n- During construction, it uses `FilterChainHelper::processFilters()` (source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h) to process the HTTP filters configuration.\\n- `processFilters()` iterates through each filter in the config and:\\n  - Retrieves the factory from the registry using `Config::Utility::getAndCheckFactory<>`\\n  - Creates a `FilterConfigProvider` using `filter_config_provider_manager_.createStaticFilterConfigProvider()`\\n  - For dynamic filters, creates `HttpDynamicFilterConfigProviderImpl` (source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h) which manages runtime filter config updates\\n\\n**Key Data Structure** (source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h line 185-189):\\n```cpp\\nstruct NamedHttpFilterFactoryCb {\\n  std::string name;                    // Canonical filter name\\n  Http::FilterFactoryCb factory_cb;   // Factory function\\n};\\n```\\n\\n### 4. Dynamic Filter Configuration\\n\\n**Runtime Updates** (source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h line 195-229):\\n- `HttpDynamicFilterConfigProviderImpl` manages filters that can be updated at runtime via xDS.\\n- When a config update arrives, `instantiateFilterFactory()` is called (line 221-229):\\n  - Looks up the factory in the registry using `Registry::FactoryRegistry<>::getFactoryByType()`\\n  - Calls `factory->createFilterFactoryFromProto()` with the new config\\n  - Returns a `NamedHttpFilterFactoryCb` containing the filter name and updated factory callback\\n\\n### Summary Flow\\n\\n1. **Initialization**: `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` constructor processes HTTP filters config via `FilterChainHelper::processFilters()`, creating `FilterConfigProvider` instances that hold factory callbacks.\\n\\n2. **Stream Creation**: When a new HTTP stream is created, `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` is called.\\n\\n3. **Chain Assembly**: `FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()` retrieves each filter's factory callback and calls `FilterManager::applyFilterFactoryCb()`.\\n\\n4. **Filter Instantiation**: The factory callback is invoked with `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl`, which instantiates actual filter objects and adds them to the chain.\\n\\n5. **Dynamic Updates**: `HttpDynamicFilterConfigProviderImpl` handles xDS config changes by looking up factories in the registry and calling `instantiateFilterFactory()` to create new filter callbacks.\\n\\nThis design separates configuration processing (factory lookup) from per-connection instantiation, allowing efficient reuse of static factory configurations for each new stream.\"\n}\n",

follows a two-stage model: static registration at initialization and per-connection instantiation at runtime.\\n\\n### 1. Filter Factory Registry and Registration\\n\\n**Core Interface** (envoy/server/filter_config.h):\\n- `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory` - Base interface for HTTP filter factories. Each HTTP filter implements a config factory that extends this interface.\\n- `UpstreamHttpFilterConfigFactory` - Parallel interface for upstream-specific HTTP filters.\\n\\nFilters are registered statically using `Registry::RegisterFactory<FilterConfigType, NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory>()`. The registry (Registry::FactoryRegistry<NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory>) stores factories indexed by their type name.\\n\\n### 2. Factory Callback and Filter Instantiation\\n\\n**Core Types** (envoy/http/filter_factory.h):\\n- `FilterFactoryCb` - Function type `std::function<void(FilterChainFactoryCallbacks&)>` that creates and installs filters for a stream. Factories return this callback during initialization.\\n- `FilterChainManager` - Abstract interface with `applyFilterFactoryCb()` method, implemented per-connection to manage filter instantiation.\\n- `FilterChainFactory` - Interface for creating filter chains, with `createFilterChain()` called when new streams arrive.\\n\\n### 3. Configuration and Filter Chain Creation\\n\\n**Configuration Processing** (source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.h and config.cc):\\n- `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` implements `Http::FilterChainFactory`.\\n- During construction, it uses `FilterChainHelper::processFilters()` (source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h) to process the HTTP filters configuration.\\n- `processFilters()` iterates through each filter in the config and:\\n  - Retrieves the factory from the registry using `Config::Utility::getAndCheckFactory<>`\\n  - Creates a `FilterConfigProvider` using `filter_config_provider_manager_.createStaticFilterConfigProvider()`\\n  - For dynamic filters, creates `HttpDynamicFilterConfigProviderImpl` (source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h) which manages runtime filter config updates\\n\\n**Key Data Structure** (source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h line 185-189):\\n```cpp\\nstruct NamedHttpFilterFactoryCb {\\n  std::string name;                    // Canonical filter name\\n  Http::FilterFactoryCb factory_cb;   // Factory function\\n};\\n```\\n\\n### 4. Per-Connection Filter Chain Creation\\n\\n**Stream Creation** (source/common/http/filter_manager.h and filter_manager.cc):\\n- `FilterManager` implements `FilterChainManager` and manages filters for a single stream.\\n- When a new stream is created, `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` is called (line 1550).\\n- This calls `filter_chain_factory_.createFilterChain(*this, false, options)` where the factory is the `HttpConnectionManagerConfig`.\\n\\n**Filter Chain Utility** (source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.cc line 17-47):\\n- `FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()` iterates through the pre-configured `FilterFactoriesList`.\\n- For each filter config provider, it retrieves the current filter factory callback via `provider->config()`.\\n- It calls `manager.applyFilterFactoryCb()` with the filter factory callback and filter context.\\n\\n**Per-Stream Filter Instantiation** (source/common/http/filter_manager.cc line 551-553):\\n```cpp\\nvoid FilterManager::applyFilterFactoryCb(FilterContext context, FilterFactoryCb& factory) {\\n  FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl callbacks(*this, context);\\n  factory(callbacks);\\n}\\n```\\nThe factory callback is invoked with a `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl` object that the factory uses to call `callbacks.addStreamFilter()`, `callbacks.addStreamDecoderFilter()`, etc., to instantiate actual filter objects.\\n\\n### 5. Dynamic Filter Configuration\\n\\n**Runtime Updates** (source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h line 195-229):\\n- `HttpDynamicFilterConfigProviderImpl` manages filters that can be updated at runtime via xDS.\\n- When a config update arrives, `instantiateFilterFactory()` is called (line 221-229):\\n  - Looks up the factory in the registry using `Registry::FactoryRegistry<>::getFactoryByType()`\\n  - Calls `factory->createFilterFactoryFromProto()` with the new config\\n  - Returns a `NamedHttpFilterFactoryCb` containing the filter name and updated factory callback\\n\\n### Summary Flow\\n\\n1. **Initialization**: `HttpConnectionManagerConfig` constructor processes HTTP filters config via `FilterChainHelper::processFilters()`, creating `FilterConfigProvider` instances that hold factory callbacks.\\n\\n2. **Stream Creation**: When a new HTTP stream is created, `FilterManager::createFilterChain()` is called.\\n\\n3. **Chain Assembly**: `FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()` retrieves each filter's factory callback and calls `FilterManager::applyFilterFactoryCb()`.\\n\\n4. **Filter Instantiation**: The factory callback is invoked with `FilterChainFactoryCallbacksImpl`, which instantiates actual filter objects and adds them to the chain.\\n\\n5. **Dynamic Updates**: `HttpDynamicFilterConfigProviderImpl` handles xDS config changes by looking up factories in the registry and calling `instantiateFilterFactory()` to create new filter callbacks.\\n\\nThis design separates configuration processing (factory lookup) from per-connection instantiation, allowing efficient reuse of static factory configurations for each new stream.\"\n}\n",
